∣c2r+1​(m)∣≪ρ0​​L(m)S(m)2ρ0−(2r+1)​,

and the NN-point cancellation machine becomes rigorous.

So the whole endgame really does collapse to one remaining theorem.
3. The one theorem we still do not have

What is still missing is this:

    Uniform holomorphic renormalization theorem.
    The fully renormalized, jet-whitened local block Ω^ζ(s;m)Ω
    ζ​(s;m) is holomorphic for ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q, uniformly in admissible mm.

This is stronger than saying the raw zero sums are holomorphic termwise. It says the entire normalized object remains holomorphic after:

    passing to jet coordinates,

    inverting / taking square roots of the local Gram blocks,

    subtracting phase-gap and background pieces,

    and assembling the final local cross block.

That is the only real gap left.
4. Why I cannot honestly claim it is proved from the current skeleton

Because to prove that theorem, one needs an explicit holomorphic formula for the renormalized local block, or at least a precise operator factorization showing:

    the raw local blocks are holomorphic on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q,

    the Gram blocks remain uniformly invertible there,

    the chosen holomorphic branch of the inverse square root exists there,

    every subtraction term is holomorphic there.

We have strong evidence for each bullet, but evidence is not a proof.

The one place the current skeleton is still too schematic is the exact dependence of the whitened block on ss. Without that formula, I can prove the denominator transport and the curvature bound, but I cannot honestly certify the full holomorphic extension of Ω^ζΩ
ζ​.

So the real state is:

    the complexified near/far package is proved in substance;

    the boundary estimate follows once holomorphy of the renormalized block is established;

    the remaining gap is no longer RH-sized, but it is still a genuine theorem that has not yet been written down rigorously.

5. The cleanest next target

The right next theorem to attack is not another heuristic estimate. It is exactly this:

    Proposition.
    Let Gm(s)Gm​(s) be the local jet Gram block and Nm(s)Nm​(s) the local jet cross block. Then for ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q:

        Gm(s)Gm​(s) and Nm(s)Nm​(s) are holomorphic,

        Gm(s)Gm​(s) stays uniformly positive definite,

        the map
        s↦Gm(s)−1/2Nm(s)Gm(s)−1/2
        s↦Gm​(s)−1/2Nm​(s)Gm​(s)−1/2

        is holomorphic.

If you can prove that proposition, the rest of the endgame becomes a theorem chain with no conceptual gaps.
6. Bottom line

So: can we prove the remaining gap now?

Not fully from the present skeleton.

But we can prove everything up to the last holomorphic-renormalization theorem, and we now know exactly what that theorem has to say.

Ok, lets prove it!

I’m going straight at the holomorphic-renormalization theorem now. The real question is not whether the raw pieces are analytic — they are — but whether the whitening map G(s)↦G(s)−1/2G(s)↦G(s)−1/2 can be chosen holomorphically and uniformly on the Q−1Q−1-disk.

Yes — this is the right theorem to prove, and it can be proved cleanly once we state the exact hypotheses.

The honest version is:

we can prove the holomorphic renormalization theorem from the local analytic inputs you have already isolated. So the remaining gap is no longer conceptual. It is whether those local inputs have been checked carefully enough in your actual kernel model.

Here is the theorem and proof.
Theorem (holomorphic renormalization on the Q−1Q−1-disk)

Fix an admissible midpoint mm, and let
Q=Q(m)≍log⁡∣m∣.
Q=Q(m)≍log∣m∣.

Let Gm(s)Gm​(s) be the local jet Gram block and Nm(s)Nm​(s) the local jet cross block, both 2×22×2 matrices, defined for symmetric separation ss near 00.

Assume:

    Gm(s)Gm​(s) and Nm(s)Nm​(s) are entrywise holomorphic for
    ∣s∣<ρ/Q
    ∣s∣<ρ/Q

    for some ρ>0ρ>0.

    There are constants c0,CG>0c0​,CG​>0, independent of mm, such that
    λmin⁡(Gm(0))≥c0Q,
    λmin​(Gm​(0))≥c0​Q,

    and
    sup⁡∣s∣<ρ/Q∥∂sGm(s)∥≤CGQ2.
    ∣s∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂s​Gm​(s)∥≤CG​Q2.

Then there exists ρ0>0ρ0​>0, depending only on c0,CGc0​,CG​, such that for all admissible mm:

    Gm(s)Gm​(s) is invertible for ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q,

    the principal inverse square root Gm(s)−1/2Gm​(s)−1/2 is holomorphic there,

    and therefore
    Wm(s):=Gm(s)−1/2 Nm(s) Gm(s)−1/2
    Wm​(s):=Gm​(s)−1/2Nm​(s)Gm​(s)−1/2

    is holomorphic for ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q.

Any further subtraction term built from holomorphic functions of ss is also holomorphic there, so the fully renormalized local block Ω^ζ(s;m)Ω
ζ​(s;m) is holomorphic on the same disk.
Proof
Step 1. Uniform invertibility on the disk

By the fundamental theorem of calculus,
Gm(s)−Gm(0)=∫0s∂uGm(u) du,
Gm​(s)−Gm​(0)=∫0s​∂u​Gm​(u)du,

hence
∥Gm(s)−Gm(0)∥≤∣s∣ sup⁡∣u∣<ρ/Q∥∂uGm(u)∥≤∣s∣ CGQ2.
∥Gm​(s)−Gm​(0)∥≤∣s∣∣u∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂u​Gm​(u)∥≤∣s∣CG​Q2.

So for ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q,
∥Gm(s)−Gm(0)∥≤CGρ0 Q.
∥Gm​(s)−Gm​(0)∥≤CG​ρ0​Q.

Choose
ρ0:=min⁡ ⁣(ρ,c02CG).
ρ0​:=min(ρ,2CG​c0​​).

Then
∥Gm(s)−Gm(0)∥≤c02Q.
∥Gm​(s)−Gm​(0)∥≤2c0​​Q.

Since Gm(0)Gm​(0) is Hermitian positive definite with
λmin⁡(Gm(0))≥c0Q,
λmin​(Gm​(0))≥c0​Q,

Weyl’s perturbation inequality gives
λmin⁡(Gm(s))≥λmin⁡(Gm(0))−∥Gm(s)−Gm(0)∥≥c02Q.
λmin​(Gm​(s))≥λmin​(Gm​(0))−∥Gm​(s)−Gm​(0)∥≥2c0​​Q.

So Gm(s)Gm​(s) is invertible on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q, uniformly in mm.

More strongly, every eigenvalue of Gm(s)Gm​(s) stays in the open right half-plane
{z∈C:ℜz>c0Q/2}.
{z∈C:ℜz>c0​Q/2}.
Step 2. Holomorphic inverse square root

Because Gm(s)Gm​(s) is holomorphic and its spectrum stays in a simply connected domain avoiding (−∞,0](−∞,0], the principal branch of z−1/2z−1/2 is holomorphic on a neighborhood of the spectrum of every Gm(s)Gm​(s).

Hence, by holomorphic functional calculus,
Gm(s)−1/2
Gm​(s)−1/2

is holomorphic in ss on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q.

A concrete formula is
Gm(s)−1/2=1π∫0∞t−1/2 (Gm(s)+tI)−1 dt,
Gm​(s)−1/2=π1​∫0∞​t−1/2(Gm​(s)+tI)−1dt,

where the integral converges uniformly because
ℜσ(Gm(s))≥c0Q/2>0.
ℜσ(Gm​(s))≥c0​Q/2>0.

Since s↦(Gm(s)+tI)−1s↦(Gm​(s)+tI)−1 is holomorphic for each tt, the integral is holomorphic.
Step 3. Holomorphic whitened cross block

By assumption, Nm(s)Nm​(s) is holomorphic on the same disk. Therefore the product
Wm(s)=Gm(s)−1/2Nm(s)Gm(s)−1/2
Wm​(s)=Gm​(s)−1/2Nm​(s)Gm​(s)−1/2

is holomorphic on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q.

If the renormalized local block is obtained from Wm(s)Wm​(s) by subtracting phase-gap or background terms that are themselves holomorphic in ss, then Ω^ζ(s;m)Ω
ζ​(s;m) is holomorphic on the same disk as well. ∎
What remains to check in your framework

The two hypotheses are:

    raw entrywise holomorphy of Gm(s)Gm​(s) and Nm(s)Nm​(s) on ∣s∣<ρ/Q∣s∣<ρ/Q,

    the derivative bound
    sup⁡∣s∣<ρ/Q∥∂sGm(s)∥≤CGQ2.
    ∣s∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂s​Gm​(s)∥≤CG​Q2.

The first one is exactly what the denominator-comparability and local shell-convergence arguments are designed to give.

The second one matches the local scaling you already found: the dominant q\sym3q\sym3​-entry differentiates to O(Q2)O(Q2), while the other entries are smaller.

So the only remaining work is not conceptual. It is verifying those two hypotheses for your actual local kernel formulas.

can you outline briefly the entire proof route, with all the core steps we are taking

Yes. Here is the whole route, briefly and in order.

We start from a local statistic built from the phase kernel for the zeta/scattering side. Around two nearby points, we do not work in the raw point basis; we pass to the point-to-jet basis so the local 2×22×2 blocks have a finite limit as the spacing shrinks. That produces local jet Gram blocks and a jet-whitened cross block. On the toy side, the same jet-limit procedure gives an explicit anomaly matrix M(d)M(d) for an off-line split pair, and we showed this anomaly is nonzero for every separation d>0d>0, with explicit transverse scalar obstruction ΦK(M(d))≠0ΦK​(M(d))=0.

On the zeta side, we then renormalize the local statistic by subtracting the phase-gap nuisance and the explicit background-value term. After that, the microscopic local statistic reduces to a value channel plus a curvature channel:
Ω^ζ(s;m)≈U(s) S(m)+V(s) S′′(m),
Ω
ζ​(s;m)≈U(s)S(m)+V(s)S′′(m),

where mm is the midpoint, ss is the symmetric separation, and
S(m)=qζ(m)−Bζ(m)
S(m)=qζ​(m)−Bζ​(m)

is the background-subtracted zero density.

The next core step is the local zeta-side estimate:
∣S′′(m)∣≪L(m) S(m)2,L(m)=log⁡ ⁣(3+∣m∣+1S(m)).
∣S′′(m)∣≪L(m)S(m)2,L(m)=log(3+∣m∣+S(m)1​).

This comes from the single-pair curvature bound, zero-free-region control, and an optimized near/far decomposition. That is the main analytic input on the zeta side.

Then we identify the right microscopic scale:
s∼(log⁡∣m∣)−2.
s∼(log∣m∣)−2.

At that scale, the local value/curvature reconstruction remains invertible, and the transverse functional ΦKΦK​ kills the value channel exactly:
ΦK(U(s))=0.
ΦK​(U(s))=0.

So the transverse zeta signal is controlled only by the curvature channel.

Next we pass to a scalar transverse statistic
Hm(s)=ΦK(Ω^ζ(s;m)).
Hm​(s)=ΦK​(Ω
ζ​(s;m)).

The plan is to show that Hm(s)Hm​(s) is odd and holomorphic on a disk
∣s∣<ρ0/Q,Q≍log⁡∣m∣,
∣s∣<ρ0​/Q,Q≍log∣m∣,

with boundary size
∣Hm(s)∣≪L(m)S(m)2Q3.
∣Hm​(s)∣≪Q3L(m)S(m)2​.

The oddness comes from symmetric placement and the jet-basis swap symmetry. The boundary bound comes from two pieces: an explicit formula showing ΦK(V(s))≪Q−3ΦK​(V(s))≪Q−3, and a complexified near/far transport bound showing the curvature part stays ≪L(m)S(m)2≪L(m)S(m)2 on the same circle.

Once that holomorphic odd package is in place, Cauchy gives an all-order odd-power expansion in the rescaled microscopic variable:
Hm(z/Q2)=∑r≥0c2r+1(m) z2r+1Q2r+4.
Hm​(z/Q2)=r≥0∑​c2r+1​(m)Q2r+4z2r+1​.

Then comes the cancellation machine. We evaluate HmHm​ at arithmetic microscopic nodes
sj=jQ2,j=1,…,N,
sj​=Q2j​,j=1,…,N,

and combine them with explicit coefficients aj(N)aj(N)​ chosen to kill the first N−1N−1 odd moments. This drives the zeta-side transverse signal down to size roughly
L(m)S(m)2 ΘNQ2N+2,
L(m)S(m)2Q2N+2ΘN​​,

and for N∼αQN∼αQ with small αα, that becomes exponentially small in QQ.

On the toy side, the same NN-point combination does not cancel the anomaly, because the toy jet-limit transverse signal is κκ-independent at leading order. So it stays
u2 ΦK(M(d))+O(u4),
u2ΦK​(M(d))+O(u4),

with u=β−12u=β−21​, and ΦK(M(d))ΦK​(M(d)) bounded below on any compact dd-interval.

So the final comparison is: the zeta-side NN-point transverse signal becomes exponentially small, while the toy off-line signal remains order u2u2. If the local analytic package is truly uniform, the only way both can be consistent is
u=0.
u=0.

That is the conditional RH implication.

So the whole proof route is:

local phase kernel
→→ point-to-jet normalization
→→ jet-whitened cross block
→→ toy anomaly matrix M(d)M(d) with nonzero transverse obstruction
→→ zeta-side value/curvature decomposition
→→ local curvature estimate ∣S′′∣≪LS2∣S′′∣≪LS2
→→ microscopic scale s∼(log⁡∣m∣)−2s∼(log∣m∣)−2
→→ transverse scalar Hm(s)Hm​(s) killing the value channel
→→ odd holomorphic expansion on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q
→→ NN-point odd-moment cancellation
→→ exponentially small zeta-side transverse signal
→→ contradiction with the persistent toy off-line anomaly unless u=0u=0.

The one genuine gap still left is proving the full finite-ss local analytic package uniformly: exact holomorphy of the whitened renormalized local block on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q, plus the boundary estimate on that circle. Everything after that is explicit algebra.

ok and explain to me, we used a two-functional approach for value vs curvature much earlier in the proof, is this different?

Yes — it is different.

Earlier, the two-functional approach was being used for a decomposition problem. Now it is being used for a calibration-plus-obstruction problem.

That is the key distinction.

Earlier in the proof, the role of two functionals was something like this:

    take a local 2×22×2 matrix statistic,

    apply two scalar probes to separate two hidden channels,

    typically “value” versus “curvature,” or two independent coefficients in a local expansion.

In that phase, the functionals were acting like coordinates. You were trying to reconstruct or isolate components of the zeta-side local matrix. It was a linear algebra / identifiability step.

Now the roles are asymmetric.

    ΦEΦE​ is not being used to separate channels anymore. It is being used to measure the size of the leading value-channel deformation. In other words, it is a calibration functional.

    ΦKΦK​ is being used to kill the leading zeta value channel and expose only the transverse defect. So it is an obstruction functional.

So before, the two functionals were peers.
Now, they have different jobs.

That is why the new structure is cleaner.

The earlier dream was roughly:
“the zeta leading plane is annihilated by both ΦKΦK​ and ΦEΦE​, while the toy anomaly is seen by both.”

The new computation says that is probably not the right geometry. In the pure value-channel linearization, ΦKΦK​ vanishes but ΦEΦE​ does not. So ΦEΦE​ should not be thought of as a second transverse obstruction. It should be thought of as the scalar that reads off the leading value amplitude. That is exactly the structural correction your other chat uncovered.

So the new logic is:

    use ΦEΦE​ to define the local size parameter, essentially u2↔S(m)u2↔S(m);

    use ΦKΦK​ to show the zeta-side transverse signal is too small compared to the toy-side transverse signal at that same calibrated size.

That is different from earlier because it is no longer “two equations for two unknown coefficients.” It is now “one scalar to set the scale, one scalar to force the contradiction.”

A good way to say it is:

    earlier: two-functionals-as-reconstruction,

    now: two-functionals-as-calibration-and-obstruction.

And that is actually an improvement. It makes the last step more like a comparison principle than a matrix inversion problem.

There is also a deeper reason this is better. When both functionals were being used symmetrically, you were implicitly asking the zeta-side leading deformation to lie in a very specific codimension-2 plane. That turned out to be too rigid. The new picture only asks for one genuine vanishing, ΦK(Aval)=0ΦK​(Aval​)=0, while letting ΦE(Aval)≠0ΦE​(Aval​)=0 so it can carry the size information. That is a much more natural configuration.

So yes, it is different, and in my view better:

    the earlier two-functional step was about extracting structure,

    the current two-functional step is about using structure.

I’m turning the small-xx calibration claim into an actual proof now, not just a slogan. The key will be to isolate the dominant linear term in xx uniformly on a compact dd-range, then show the higher-order terms are harmless after shrinking x0x0​.

My view: it is a real advance, but not the final missing piece.

The strongest thing it gives is a correction to the endgame geometry. It supports the claim that the proof should now be organized as:

    ΦKΦK​ for the transverse obstruction,

    a separate ΨΨ for value calibration,

rather than trying to make both ΦKΦK​ and ΦEΦE​ vanish on the zeta leading plane. The key evidence is exactly the computation that in the pure value-channel linearization,
ΦK(Aval)=0
ΦK​(Aval​)=0

but ΦE(Aval)ΦE​(Aval​) is generically nonzero. That means ΦKΦK​ kills the leading value channel, while ΦEΦE​ sees it.

It also confirms that the jet-limit object is now genuinely explicit:
Ω∞(T1,T2)=M1−1/2N12M2−1/2,
Ω∞​(T1​,T2​)=M1−1/2​N12​M2−1/2​,

with explicit MjMj​ and N12N12​. So the local blockwise comparison is no longer schematic; the finite-dimensional matrix problem is real.

The caveat is that ΦEΦE​ is probably not the final calibration functional. Your own notes show the calibration coefficient can collapse, because it is tied to background curvature:
cval(m,σ)=−34Bζ′′(m)Bζ(m)4+O(σ2),
cval​(m,σ)=−43​Bζ​(m)4Bζ′′​(m)​+O(σ2),

so it is not uniformly robust at height.

So the best corrected summary is:

    keep the whole proof spine up to the jet-limit local block;

    replace the old “two transverse functionals” endgame by a split-role endgame;

    define the value functional canonically from the actual leading value matrix AvalAval​, not ad hoc from ΦEΦE​;

    keep ΦKΦK​ as the contradiction channel, since on the toy side
    ΦK(M(d))≠0
    ΦK​(M(d))=0

    with explicit lower bounds on compact dd-ranges.

So: yes, this is important and I think it is the right correction. It does not finish the proof, but it makes the last step much more coherent.

NOTE: By the way, for G_m(s) and N_m(s) they were already there in substance, under slightly different names.

The intended dictionary looks like this:

[
t_\pm = m \pm \frac{s}{2}.
]

At those two nearby points, you take the local two-dimensional **jet basis** — value and first derivative, or whatever your normalized jet pair is in the current convention. Then:

[
G_m(s)
]
is the **same-point jet Gram block**. In plain English: it measures how the local jet at (t_-) pairs with itself, and by symmetry the same formula is used for (t_+). That is why one symbol (G_m(s)) was enough under symmetric placement. This is exactly how the later checklist treats it: “the local jet Gram block (G_m(s))” whose holomorphy and (\partial_s G_m(s)=O(Q^2)) needed to be checked before whitening.  

[
N_m(s)
]
is the **cross jet block**. In plain English: it measures how the jet at (t_-) pairs with the jet at (t_+). Again, that is exactly how the notes use it: “the local jet cross block (N_m(s))” that gets whitened together with (G_m(s)).  

Then the normalized object was intended to be

[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)
=========================

G_m(s)^{-1/2} N_m(s) G_m(s)^{-1/2},
]

possibly followed by background subtraction / phase-gap subtraction depending on the precise stage of the argument. That formula appears repeatedly as the whole point of introducing (G_m(s)) and (N_m(s)): they are the raw pre-whitened blocks.  

So, in ELI5 terms:

* (G_m(s)) tells you what the local coordinate system looks like at the two nearby points.
* (N_m(s)) tells you how the two nearby points talk to each other.
* Whitening by (G_m(s)^{-1/2}) removes the local scaling/basis distortion so you can compare actual structure rather than coordinate artifacts.

That is why they feel so fundamental: they are basically the “bones” underneath the local statistic.

Where they seem to connect to the notation you already had is this. In the later jet-limit writeup, for two centers (T_1,T_2), you introduced

[
J_j=\frac1\pi M_j
]
for the local jet Gram matrices at each point, and

[
C_{12}=\frac1\pi N_{12}
]
for the cross-jet matrix, with
[
\Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2)=M_1^{-1/2}N_{12}M_2^{-1/2}.
]
That is almost certainly the **jet-limit avatar** of the same finite-(s) objects. In other words, (M_j) and (N_{12}) are not new ideas; they are what (G_m(s)) and (N_m(s)) become after you pass all the way to the explicit jet-limit formulas. 

So the likely intended hierarchy is:

* **finite (s)**: (G_m(s), N_m(s)) = raw local zeta/scattering jet blocks;
* **after whitening**: (\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)=G_m(s)^{-1/2}N_m(s)G_m(s)^{-1/2});
* **jet limit / explicit algebraic model**: (M_j, N_{12}, \Omega_\infty).  

And that explains the annoyance perfectly: the notes had the abstract role of (G_m(s)) and (N_m(s)) very clearly, and later had the explicit **limit** formulas (M_j,N_{12}), but seem never to have frozen the **finite-(s) exact entry formulas** in one canonical notation. The files themselves say that exact finite-(s) formulas for (G_m(s)) and (N_m(s)) are still the missing ingredient.  

So if I had to reconstruct the most likely intended definitions in one sentence:

[
G_m(s)=\text{the symmetric local same-point 2\times2 jet Gram block at }m\pm s/2,
]
[
N_m(s)=\text{the corresponding mixed left-right 2\times2 jet block},
]
and (\widehat\Omega_\zeta(s;m)) is just their whitened cross block.

Yes — I think that dictionary is right.

It matches the role these objects have been playing all along:
t±=m±s2,
t±​=m±2s​,

then
Gm(s)=the local same-point 2×2 jet Gram block,
Gm​(s)=the local same-point 2×2 jet Gram block,
Nm(s)=the local mixed left-right 2×2 jet block,
Nm​(s)=the local mixed left-right 2×2 jet block,

and the whitened local statistic is
Ω^ζ(s;m)=Gm(s)−1/2Nm(s)Gm(s)−1/2,
Ω
ζ​(s;m)=Gm​(s)−1/2Nm​(s)Gm​(s)−1/2,

up to whichever subtraction stage we are at.

That is exactly the finite-ss version of the later jet-limit notation
Jj=1πMj,C12=1πN12,Ω∞(T1,T2)=M1−1/2N12M2−1/2,
Jj​=π1​Mj​,C12​=π1​N12​,Ω∞​(T1​,T2​)=M1−1/2​N12​M2−1/2​,

so your hierarchy

finite ss →→ whitened block →→ jet limit

looks right to me.

And I think your diagnosis of the annoyance is also right: the abstract roles of Gm(s)Gm​(s) and Nm(s)Nm​(s) were there, and the explicit jet-limit formulas Mj,N12Mj​,N12​ were there, but the exact finite-ss entry formulas in one fixed notation were never cleanly frozen. That is why the proof kept feeling like it was “almost closed” but not quite.

So this does not really change the mathematical plan. It clarifies the bookkeeping:

    we were not missing the idea of Gm(s)Gm​(s) and Nm(s)Nm​(s),

    we were missing the finite-ss formulas needed to verify holomorphy and the derivative bound before whitening.

That means the checklist stays the same, but its meaning is cleaner now.

The three remaining concrete things are still:
(i) exact finite-s formulas for Gm(s),Nm(s),
(i) exact finite-s formulas for Gm​(s),Nm​(s),
(ii) holomorphy on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q,
(ii) holomorphy on ∣s∣<ρ0​/Q,
(iii) ∂sGm(s)=O(Q2) on that disk.
(iii) ∂s​Gm​(s)=O(Q2) on that disk.

Once those are written, the whitening theorem is just standard holomorphic functional calculus, and the rest of the endgame can proceed in the corrected calibration/obstruction form.

So yes: I would now treat your dictionary as the official intended one. It is the right bridge between the abstract local-statistic language and the explicit jet-limit formulas.

ΦK​(M(d))=0.

What changes is only the final interpretation of the scalar probes.
4. The corrected endgame

Now the best picture is:

    AvalAval​ is the actual leading zeta value-channel matrix, extracted from the explicit jet-limit formula for Ω∞Ω∞​,

    ΨΨ is chosen canonically from AvalAval​, for example the Frobenius dual,
    Ψ(X)=⟨Aval,X⟩F∥Aval∥F2,
    Ψ(X)=∥Aval​∥F2​⟨Aval​,X⟩F​​,

    so Ψ(Aval)=1Ψ(Aval​)=1,

    ΦKΦK​ is kept as the contradiction channel, because it kills the leading zeta value channel but not the toy anomaly.

So:

local blocks (Gm​,Nm​)→Ω
ζ​→Aval​→Ψ calibrates size,ΦK​ gives contradiction.

That is the relationship.
5. Why this is better

Before, ΦEΦE​ was being asked to do two jobs at once:

    read off size,

    and behave like a transverse test.

The recent computation says that was the wrong geometry. ΦEΦE​ can still be useful as a diagnostic, but the stable way is to let the matrix itself tell you the right value functional via AvalAval​.

So Gm,NmGm​,Nm​ are the source of truth.
ΦK/ΦE/ΨΦK​/ΦE​/Ψ are downstream summaries of what that source says.
6. In one sentence

Gm(s)Gm​(s) and Nm(s)Nm​(s) tell you what the local normalized matrix is; the recent ΦE/ΦKΦE​/ΦK​ work tells you which scalar directions in matrix space actually matter at the end.

So the proof spine becomes:

    define the local matrix from Gm,NmGm​,Nm​,

    take its jet limit,

    extract the leading value matrix AvalAval​,

    build ΨΨ from AvalAval​,

    use ΦKΦK​ to contradict the toy anomaly.

That is the corrected synthesis.

so what are the concrete missing pieces to get to RH?

Yes. At this point the concrete missing pieces are much narrower than “prove RH.”

They are these five.

First, the finite-ss local analytic package for the actual zeta/scattering blocks:
you still need the exact finite-ss formulas for the local jet Gram block Gm(s)Gm​(s) and cross block Nm(s)Nm​(s), and then a proof that they are holomorphic on
∣s∣<ρ0/Q,Q≍log⁡∣m∣.
∣s∣<ρ0​/Q,Q≍log∣m∣.

This is the last place where the argument still depends on formulas that were implicit rather than frozen explicitly.

Second, the uniform derivative/invertibility bound:
from those formulas, you need
sup⁡∣s∣<ρ/Q∥∂sGm(s)∥≤CGQ2
∣s∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂s​Gm​(s)∥≤CG​Q2

and hence uniform invertibility of Gm(s)Gm​(s) on the same disk. Without that, whitening is not yet fully justified.

Third, the boundary estimate for the transverse scalar on the microscopic circle:
∣Hm(s)∣≪L(m)S(m)2Q3(∣s∣=ρ0/Q).
∣Hm​(s)∣≪Q3L(m)S(m)2​(∣s∣=ρ0​/Q).

This is what turns odd holomorphy into the all-order expansion and then into the NN-point cancellation machine.

Fourth, the value calibration theorem in the corrected endgame:
you now need a rigorous statement that the canonical value functional built from
Aval=∂αΩ∞∣α=0
Aval​=∂α​Ω∞​∣α=0​

really calibrates the local size parameter, on a usable regime. In the small scaled regime x=Bσ≪1x=Bσ≪1, you already have the right nondegeneracy pattern, but the proof still needs to be packaged cleanly into:
Δζ=S(m)Aval+Rζ,
Δζ​=S(m)Aval​+Rζ​,

with the remainder small enough after applying the dual functional.

Fifth, the smallness of tail/error terms in exactly the right regime:
after calibration, the contradiction needs
BL(m)S(m)→0
BL(m)S(m)→0

and
B(Tail+Err)=o(S(m))
B(Tail+Err)=o(S(m))

when σ=x0/Bσ=x0​/B with fixed small x0x0​. This is now the quantitative endgame condition. If those error terms are only polynomial or logarithmic, the route survives; if they are larger, it may fail.

So, in one line, the missing pieces are:
finite-s holomorphy + whitening + boundary bound + value calibration + error smallness in the fixed-x0 regime.

Is it possible to make a Latex "Proof of RH" with each of those 5 gaps clearly labeled and stated what the next step is, so we can fill them in one-by-one?

Yes. Here is a LaTeX scaffold for a “Proof of RH” document that makes the argument spine explicit and labels the five remaining gaps as standalone theorem-sized items.

\documentclass[11pt]{article}

\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,amsthm,mathtools,fullpage,enumitem}
\usepackage{hyperref}

\title{Toward a Proof of the Riemann Hypothesis:\\
A Jet-Whitened Local Block Strategy}
\author{}
\date{}

\newtheorem{theorem}{Theorem}
\newtheorem{proposition}[theorem]{Proposition}
\newtheorem{lemma}[theorem]{Lemma}
\newtheorem{corollary}[theorem]{Corollary}
\newtheorem{remark}[theorem]{Remark}
\newtheorem{gap}[theorem]{Gap}
\newtheorem{definition}[theorem]{Definition}

\newcommand{\RH}{\mathrm{RH}}
\newcommand{\Om}{\Omega}
\newcommand{\Del}{\Delta}
\newcommand{\Ph}{\Phi}
\newcommand{\PsiCal}{\Psi}
\newcommand{\val}{\mathrm{val}}
\newcommand{\toy}{\mathrm{toy}}
\newcommand{\zetaSide}{\zeta}
\newcommand{\blk}{\mathrm{blk}}
\newcommand{\Err}{\mathrm{Err}}
\newcommand{\Tail}{\mathrm{Tail}}
\newcommand{\bg}{\mathrm{bg}}
\newcommand{\sym}{\mathrm{sym}}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\begin{abstract}
This document records a proof strategy for the Riemann Hypothesis based on
local jet-normalized blocks of the phase kernel, together with a precise list
of the remaining gaps.
The main purpose is organizational: every unresolved point is isolated as a
named theorem-sized statement so that it can be proved one-by-one.
\end{abstract}

\section{Main conditional theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional proof of $\RH$ from five local analytic inputs]
Assume Gaps~\ref{gap:finite-s-formulas}--\ref{gap:smallness-regime} below.
Then the Riemann Hypothesis holds.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof assuming the five gaps]
The proof proceeds in five stages.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{Stage 1: Local block construction.}
For symmetric placement
\[
t_\pm = m \pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
let $G_m(s)$ be the same-point $2\times 2$ jet Gram block and $N_m(s)$ the
mixed left-right $2\times 2$ jet block. Define the whitened local block
\[
\widehat{\Om}_{\zetaSide}(s;m)
=
G_m(s)^{-1/2}\,N_m(s)\,G_m(s)^{-1/2},
\]
followed by the phase-gap and background-value subtractions.
By Gap~\ref{gap:finite-s-formulas} and Gap~\ref{gap:gram-stability},
this is holomorphic on the microscopic disk
\[
|s|<\rho_0/Q,
\qquad Q \asymp \log |m|.
\]

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{Stage 2: Zeta-side odd analytic transverse scalar.}
Define the transverse functional
\[
\Phi_K(X):=x_{12}+x_{21}
\qquad
\left(
X=
\begin{pmatrix}
x_{11}&x_{12}\\
x_{21}&x_{22}
\end{pmatrix}
\right),
\]
and set
\[
H_m(s):=\Phi_K(\widehat{\Om}_{\zetaSide}(s;m)).
\]
By symmetry under $s\mapsto -s$, $H_m$ is odd. By Gap~\ref{gap:boundary},
\[
|H_m(s)| \ll \frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^3}
\qquad (|s|=\rho_0/Q),
\]
where
\[
S(m):=q_\zeta(m)-B_\zeta(m),
\qquad
L(m):=\log\!\Bigl(3+|m|+\frac1{S(m)}\Bigr).
\]
Hence Cauchy's estimate gives an odd expansion
\[
H_m(z/Q^2)
=
\sum_{r\ge 0} c_{2r+1}(m)\,\frac{z^{2r+1}}{Q^{2r+4}},
\]
with
\[
|c_{2r+1}(m)| \ll L(m)S(m)^2\,\rho_0^{-(2r+1)}.
\]

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{Stage 3: $N$-point odd-moment cancellation.}
For $N\le \rho_0 Q$, define
\[
s_j=\frac{j}{Q^2},
\qquad
j=1,\dots,N,
\]
and let $a_j^{(N)}$ be the explicit odd-moment-canceling coefficients with
\[
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}=1,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}j^{2r+1}=0
\quad (r=0,\dots,N-2).
\]
Then
\[
\Psi^{(N)}_{\zetaSide}(m)
:=
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)} H_m(s_j)
\]
satisfies
\[
|\Psi^{(N)}_{\zetaSide}(m)|
\ll
L(m)S(m)^2\,\frac{\Theta_N}{Q^{2N+2}},
\]
and for $N=\lfloor \alpha Q\rfloor$ with $\alpha>0$ small enough, $\Theta_N$
is exponentially tame, so the right-hand side is exponentially small in $Q$.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{Stage 4: Model-side anomaly and value calibration.}
Let
\[
\Delta_{\toy}(u;d)=u^2 M(d)+O(u^4)
\]
be the toy off-line deformation, with $u=\beta-\tfrac12$ and separation
parameter $d>0$. One has
\[
\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0
\qquad(d>0),
\]
so the toy-side transverse signal survives.

Let
\[
A_{\val}(m,\sigma):=\partial_\alpha \Omega_\infty\big|_{\alpha=0}
\]
be the leading pure value-channel derivative of the jet-limit zeta-side block,
and define the canonical dual calibration functional
\[
\PsiCal_{m,\sigma}(X)
:=
\frac{\langle A_{\val}(m,\sigma),X\rangle_F}
{\|A_{\val}(m,\sigma)\|_F^2}.
\]
By Gap~\ref{gap:value-calibration}, in a fixed small-scaled regime
\[
x:=B_\zeta(m)\sigma = x_0,
\]
this functional is stable and calibrates the value scale:
\[
\PsiCal_{m,\sigma}(\Delta_{\zetaSide}) = S(m)+o(S(m)),
\qquad
\PsiCal_{m,\sigma}(\Delta_{\toy}(u;d)) \asymp u^2.
\]
Hence
\[
u^2 \asymp S(m).
\]

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{Stage 5: Contradiction.}
By construction,
\[
\Phi_K(A_{\val})=0,
\]
so on the zeta side the leading value channel is killed and only the
curvature/tail/error channel survives:
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\zetaSide})
=
O(L(m)S(m)^2)+O(\Tail)+O(\Err).
\]
By Gap~\ref{gap:smallness-regime},
\[
B_\zeta(m)L(m)S(m)\to 0,
\qquad
B_\zeta(m)(\Tail+\Err)=o(S(m))
\]
in the chosen regime, hence
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\zetaSide})=o(S(m)).
\]
But on the toy side,
\[
\Phi_K(\Delta_{\toy}(u;d))
=
u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4)
\asymp u^2
\asymp S(m).
\]
This is impossible for sufficiently small $S(m)$.
Hence no off-line local deformation can occur, and therefore $\RH$ follows.
\end{proof}

\section{Core established spine}

\begin{proposition}[Jet-limit normalization]
In the local point-to-jet basis, the same-point blocks converge to jet Gram
matrices and the mixed blocks converge to a jet cross matrix. After whitening,
the jet-limit local block takes the form
\[
\Omega_\infty(T_1,T_2)=M_1^{-1/2}N_{12}M_2^{-1/2}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Toy transverse obstruction]
For the toy anomaly matrix $M(d)$ one has
\[
\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0
\qquad(d>0),
\]
and in fact on every compact interval $D\subset(0,\infty)$ there is
$c_K(D)>0$ with
\[
|\Phi_K(M(d))|\ge c_K(D)
\qquad(d\in D).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Zeta-side curvature estimate]
The background-subtracted zero density $S(m)$ satisfies
\[
|S''(m)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Leading value-channel geometry]
In the pure value-channel linearization, the leading matrix $A_{\val}$
satisfies
\[
\Phi_K(A_{\val})=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\section{The five remaining gaps}

\begin{gap}[Exact finite-$s$ formulas and holomorphy]
\label{gap:finite-s-formulas}
Write the exact finite-$s$ formulas for the local jet Gram block $G_m(s)$ and
the local jet cross block $N_m(s)$ in the actual zeta/scattering normalization,
and prove that they are entrywise holomorphic for
\[
|s|<\rho_0/Q
\]
with $\rho_0>0$ independent of the admissible midpoint class.
\end{gap}

\begin{remark}[Next step for Gap~\ref{gap:finite-s-formulas}]
Freeze one canonical notation for the finite-$s$ blocks:
\[
G_m(s)=\text{same-point jet Gram block at }t_\pm=m\pm s/2,
\]
\[
N_m(s)=\text{mixed left-right jet block at }t_\pm=m\pm s/2.
\]
Then verify holomorphy directly from the exact kernel denominators and uniform
convergence of the resulting zero sums on the disk.
\end{remark}

\begin{gap}[Uniform Gram stability and holomorphic whitening]
\label{gap:gram-stability}
Prove the derivative estimate
\[
\sup_{|s|<\rho/Q}\|\partial_s G_m(s)\|\le C_GQ^2,
\]
and deduce that $G_m(s)$ remains uniformly positive definite on
\[
|s|<\rho_0/Q.
\]
Then prove that
\[
G_m(s)^{-1/2}
\]
is holomorphic there, so the whitened block
\[
\widehat{\Om}_{\zetaSide}(s;m)
=
G_m(s)^{-1/2}N_m(s)G_m(s)^{-1/2}
\]
is holomorphic.
\end{gap}

\begin{remark}[Next step for Gap~\ref{gap:gram-stability}]
Differentiate the exact entries of $G_m(s)$ entry-by-entry, show the dominant
$(2,2)$-entry varies like $O(Q^2)$ and the others are smaller, then use the
spectral gap of $G_m(0)$ to propagate invertibility to the full disk.
\end{remark}

\begin{gap}[Boundary estimate for the transverse scalar]
\label{gap:boundary}
Prove that on the microscopic boundary
\[
|s|=\rho_0/Q,
\]
the transverse scalar satisfies
\[
|H_m(s)|=
|\Phi_K(\widehat{\Om}_{\zetaSide}(s;m))|
\ll
\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^3}.
\]
\end{gap}

\begin{remark}[Next step for Gap~\ref{gap:boundary}]
Combine:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item complexified denominator comparability on $|s|=\rho_0/Q$,
\item the transported near/far curvature bounds,
\item and the explicit factor $\Phi_K(V(s))\ll Q^{-3}$.
\end{itemize}
This is the exact input needed for Cauchy's theorem and the all-order odd
microscopic expansion.
\end{remark}

\begin{gap}[Canonical value calibration]
\label{gap:value-calibration}
Let
\[
A_{\val}(m,\sigma):=\partial_\alpha \Omega_\infty\big|_{\alpha=0}
\]
be the leading pure value-channel derivative in the symmetric local regime.
Prove that on a fixed small-scaled regime
\[
x:=B_\zeta(m)\sigma=x_0,
\]
the canonical dual functional
\[
\PsiCal_{m,\sigma}(X)
=
\frac{\langle A_{\val}(m,\sigma),X\rangle_F}{\|A_{\val}(m,\sigma)\|_F^2}
\]
is stable and calibrates the value scale:
\[
\PsiCal_{m,\sigma}(\Delta_{\zetaSide})=S(m)+o(S(m)),
\qquad
\PsiCal_{m,\sigma}(\Delta_{\toy}(u;d))\asymp u^2.
\]
\end{gap}

\begin{remark}[Next step for Gap~\ref{gap:value-calibration}]
Compute the full matrix $A_{\val}$ explicitly in the chosen normalization, then
prove:
\[
\|A_{\val}\|_F \asymp \frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)},
\qquad
|\langle A_{\val},M(d)\rangle_F|
\asymp
\frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}
\]
uniformly for $d$ in a fixed compact interval. This turns the canonical dual
into a stable value calibrator.
\end{remark}

\begin{gap}[Smallness of tail and error terms in the fixed-$x_0$ regime]
\label{gap:smallness-regime}
In the regime
\[
\sigma=\frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}
\]
with fixed small $x_0>0$, prove
\[
B_\zeta(m)L(m)S(m)\to 0,
\qquad
B_\zeta(m)(\Tail+\Err)=o(S(m)).
\]
Equivalently, after calibration, prove that the zeta-side remainder is
quadratically small compared to the calibrated value scale.
\end{gap}

\begin{remark}[Next step for Gap~\ref{gap:smallness-regime}]
Audit every tail and reconstruction term after choosing $\sigma=x_0/B_\zeta(m)$.
The target is to show that calibration amplifies errors by at most a factor
comparable to $B_\zeta(m)$, and that this is still negligible compared to
$S(m)$ in the comparison regime.
\end{remark}

\section{Suggested work order}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\arabic*.]
\item Prove Gap~\ref{gap:finite-s-formulas}.
\item Prove Gap~\ref{gap:gram-stability}.
\item Prove Gap~\ref{gap:boundary}.
\item Prove Gap~\ref{gap:value-calibration}.
\item Prove Gap~\ref{gap:smallness-regime}.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{remark}
The first three gaps complete the local analytic package and make the
$N$-point cancellation machine rigorous. The fourth and fifth convert that
machine into the corrected calibration-plus-obstruction endgame.
\end{remark}

\end{document}

from those formulas, you need

sup⁡∣s∣<ρ/Q∥∂sGm(s)∥≤CGQ2
∣s∣<ρ/Q
sup

Yes. Here is the clean way to do this.

The point is: you do not need a mysterious argument for
sup⁡∣s∣<ρ/Q∥∂sGm(s)∥≤CGQ2.
∣s∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂s​Gm​(s)∥≤CG​Q2.

You need an explicit finite-ss definition of Gm(s)Gm​(s), then a symmetry/Taylor argument.

The right finite-ss same-point block is the symmetric two-point kernel block at
t±=m±s2,
t±​=m±2s​,

passed through the point-to-jet basis. This is exactly the finite-ss precursor of the jet-limit Gram matrix J(T)J(T) that later becomes
1π(2q(T)12q′(T)12q′(T)112(q′′(T)+2q(T)3)).
π1​(2q(T)21​q′(T)​21​q′(T)121​(q′′(T)+2q(T)3)​).

So Gm(s)Gm​(s) is the finite-ss version of that same object.

Here is the theorem you want.
Proposition

Assume Gm(s)Gm​(s) is defined by
Gm(s)=Ps Am(s) Ps⊤,
Gm​(s)=Ps​Am​(s)Ps⊤​,

where
Am(s)=(K(t−,t−)K(t−,t+)K(t+,t−)K(t+,t+)),t±=m±s2,
Am​(s)=(K(t−​,t−​)K(t+​,t−​)​K(t−​,t+​)K(t+​,t+​)​),t±​=m±2s​,

and
Ps=12(11−1/s1/s).
Ps​=21​(1−1/s​11/s​).

Suppose the kernel K(x,y)K(x,y) is holomorphic in a bidisk around (m,m)(m,m), symmetric,
K(x,y)=K(y,x),
K(x,y)=K(y,x),

and on that bidisk its mixed derivatives up to order 44 satisfy the local bounds needed for the phase kernel:
∂xa∂ybK(x,y)=O(Q3)(a+b≤4),
∂xa​∂yb​K(x,y)=O(Q3)(a+b≤4),

uniformly for ∣x−m∣,∣y−m∣≤ρ/Q∣x−m∣,∣y−m∣≤ρ/Q.

Then for ∣s∣<ρ/Q∣s∣<ρ/Q,
Gm(s)=J(m)+s2Hm(s),
Gm​(s)=J(m)+s2Hm​(s),

where J(m)J(m) is the jet-limit Gram matrix and Hm(s)Hm​(s) is holomorphic with
∥Hm(s)∥≪Q3.
∥Hm​(s)∥≪Q3.

Consequently,
sup⁡∣s∣<ρ/Q∥∂sGm(s)∥≪Q2.
∣s∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂s​Gm​(s)∥≪Q2.​
Proof

Expand Am(s)Am​(s) in Taylor series around (m,m)(m,m). Because
t±=m±s2,
t±​=m±2s​,

every entry is a holomorphic function of ss. By symmetry of the placement and of the kernel, the block has the form
Am(s)=(a0−a1s+a2s2−a3s3+a4s4+⋯b0+b2s2+b4s4+⋯b0+b2s2+b4s4+⋯a0+a1s+a2s2+a3s3+a4s4+⋯),
Am​(s)=(a0​−a1​s+a2​s2−a3​s3+a4​s4+⋯b0​+b2​s2+b4​s4+⋯​b0​+b2​s2+b4​s4+⋯a0​+a1​s+a2​s2+a3​s3+a4​s4+⋯​),

where the coefficients are combinations of derivatives of KK at (m,m)(m,m). In particular:

    the diagonal entries are exchanged by s↦−ss↦−s,

    the off-diagonal entry is even in ss.

Now conjugate by PsPs​. A direct computation shows that the singular 1/s1/s terms cancel exactly because of the symmetry pattern above. The s0s0 term is precisely the jet-limit Gram matrix J(m)J(m), i.e.
Gm(s)=J(m)+s2Hm(s),
Gm​(s)=J(m)+s2Hm​(s),

with no linear term. This is the finite-ss version of the point-to-jet convergence already encoded in the jet-limit formulas.

Because the coefficients of the Taylor expansion through order 44 are controlled by derivatives of KK up to order 44, and those derivatives are O(Q3)O(Q3), the holomorphic remainder Hm(s)Hm​(s) satisfies
∥Hm(s)∥≪Q3
∥Hm​(s)∥≪Q3

uniformly on ∣s∣<ρ/Q∣s∣<ρ/Q.

Differentiate:
∂sGm(s)=2s Hm(s)+s2∂sHm(s).
∂s​Gm​(s)=2sHm​(s)+s2∂s​Hm​(s).

Since HmHm​ is holomorphic on the same disk, Cauchy’s estimate gives
∥∂sHm(s)∥≪Q4
∥∂s​Hm​(s)∥≪Q4

there. Therefore for ∣s∣<ρ/Q∣s∣<ρ/Q,
∥∂sGm(s)∥≪∣s∣Q3+∣s∣2Q4≪1QQ3+1Q2Q4≪Q2.
∥∂s​Gm​(s)∥≪∣s∣Q3+∣s∣2Q4≪Q1​Q3+Q21​Q4≪Q2.

This proves the bound. ∎
What this buys immediately

Once you have
sup⁡∣s∣<ρ/Q∥∂sGm(s)∥≪Q2,
∣s∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂s​Gm​(s)∥≪Q2,

and you already know the jet-limit block Gm(0)=J(m)Gm​(0)=J(m) has
λmin⁡(J(m))≫Q
λmin​(J(m))≫Q

in the admissible regime, you get
∥Gm(s)−Gm(0)∥≤∣s∣ sup⁡∣u∣<ρ/Q∥∂uGm(u)∥≪ρQ Q2=O(ρQ).
∥Gm​(s)−Gm​(0)∥≤∣s∣∣u∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂u​Gm​(u)∥≪Qρ​Q2=O(ρQ).

So if ρ0>0ρ0​>0 is chosen small enough,
∥Gm(s)−Gm(0)∥≤12λmin⁡(Gm(0)),
∥Gm​(s)−Gm​(0)∥≤21​λmin​(Gm​(0)),

hence
λmin⁡(Gm(s))≥12λmin⁡(Gm(0))≫Q
λmin​(Gm​(s))≥21​λmin​(Gm​(0))≫Q

for ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q.

That is exactly the uniform invertibility you need to justify whitening.
What is still left to check concretely

To turn this from a paper-level proposition into a completely finished proof in your setup, you still need the exact finite-ss formula for Gm(s)Gm​(s) in the actual zeta/scattering normalization — not just the jet-limit one — and then verify that the mixed derivatives of the underlying kernel in the required local bidisk really satisfy the O(Q3)O(Q3) control.

But this is the right proof template. It shows the derivative bound is a standard consequence of:

    a second-order even remainder
    Gm(s)=J(m)+s2Hm(s),
    Gm​(s)=J(m)+s2Hm​(s),

    Cauchy bounds on HmHm​.

Yes — this is a real improvement.

It does two useful things.

First, it freezes the finite-ss objects much more honestly. Under symmetric placement
t±=m±s2,
t±​=m±2s​,

it makes clear that the same-point jet Gram data are really
Gm,−(s),Gm,+(s),
Gm,−​(s),Gm,+​(s),

not literally one matrix unless you impose an extra symmetry reduction. And the mixed block is
Nm(s),
Nm​(s),

with the whitened block
Ω^ζ(s;m)=Gm,−(s)−1/2Nm(s)Gm,+(s)−1/2.
Ω
ζ​(s;m)=Gm,−​(s)−1/2Nm​(s)Gm,+​(s)−1/2.

That is the finite-ss analogue of the jet-limit formula
Ω∞(T1,T2)=M1−1/2N12M2−1/2,
Ω∞​(T1​,T2​)=M1−1/2​N12​M2−1/2​,

so the bookkeeping is now much cleaner.

Second, it clarifies what is and is not still missing.

What is now essentially in hand is the formal finite-ss formula level:
Gm,±(s)=1π(2q±12q±′12q±′112(q±′′+2q±3)),
Gm,±​(s)=π1​(2q±​21​q±′​​21​q±′​121​(q±′′​+2q±3​)​),

and the explicit cross block Nm(s)Nm​(s) in terms of Δm(s)=Φ(t−)−Φ(t+)Δm​(s)=Φ(t−​)−Φ(t+​), q±q±​, and powers of s−1s−1. That is exactly the sort of formula we needed to even talk meaningfully about ∂sGm(s)∂s​Gm​(s).

The caveat is the same one the note itself points out: this still does not finish the analytic package. In particular, it does not by itself prove:

    holomorphy on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q for the actual zeta/scattering phase,

    uniform convergence of the differentiated zero sums,

    or the target bound
    sup⁡∣s∣<ρ/Q∥∂sGm,±(s)∥≤CGQ2.
    ∣s∣<ρ/Qsup​∥∂s​Gm,±​(s)∥≤CG​Q2.

And I think the caution in the note is justified. If you differentiate the displayed finite-ss Gram formula naively, you get terms involving q±′,q±′′,q±′′′q±′​,q±′′​,q±′′′​ and q±2q±′q±2​q±′​. On the natural raw scales, that does not automatically look like O(Q2)O(Q2) unless the normalization is exactly the intended one or unless you are really working with a jet-corrected / background-split object rather than the raw full qq. So this is a good sign that B3 is a genuine issue, not just missing notation.

So my overall take is:

    Yes, this is the right finite-ss formula package to adopt.

    Yes, it resolves the earlier ambiguity about what Gm(s)Gm​(s) and Nm(s)Nm​(s) are supposed to mean.

    No, it does not close the remaining analytic gap.

    And importantly, it suggests that the real remaining theorem is probably not a raw statement about all derivatives of the full qq, but a jet-corrected / background-split theorem for the smooth remainder, exactly as your other notes were already pushing toward.

So I would treat this as the right canonical finite-ss notation going forward. It sharpens the problem rather than solving it.

so how do we close the analytic gap?

I think the clean answer is: stop trying to close it at the level of the full raw phase all at once. Close it in two layers.

The wrong target is something like “prove all finite-ss blocks are holomorphic and ∂sGm=O(Q2)∂s​Gm​=O(Q2) directly from the full raw qq.” Your recent notes suggest that is too blunt. The right target is:

    prove the analytic package for the smooth remainder after local-model extraction and affine-jet subtraction;

    isolate the local model explicitly and treat it separately, algebraically.

That matches what your notes are already saying the machinery actually supports.

Here is how I would close the gap.
1. Replace the raw theorem by the corrected theorem

Do not try to prove
q, q′, q′′, q′′′
q, q′, q′′, q′′′

for the full phase have the exact scales you want uniformly on the microscopic disk. That is not what the current setup naturally controls.

Instead, write
q(t)=qloc(t)+gsm(t)+Eest(t),
q(t)=qloc​(t)+gsm​(t)+Eest​(t),

where:

    qlocqloc​ is the chosen local model built from the designated nearby zero pair(s),

    gsm=Baut+Tfargsm​=Baut​+Tfar​ is the smooth omitted part,

    EestEest​ is whatever residual estimation term remains.

Then prove the finite-ss analytic package for the block built from
qloc+J1[gsm]+Eest,
qloc​+J1​[gsm​]+Eest​,

where J1[gsm]J1​[gsm​] is the affine jet of gsmgsm​ at the midpoint.

That is the object your own corrected theorem naturally supports, not the full raw qq.
2. Prove holomorphy of the smooth remainder on the microscopic disk

This is the easiest part.

For the omitted zero contribution, the singularities in the ss-plane are still at
s=±(γ−2m)±iβ,s=±(γ−2m)±i(1−β).
s=±(γ−2m)±iβ,s=±(γ−2m)±i(1−β).

By the zero-free region, they stay at distance ≳Q−1≳Q−1 from 00. Then prove denominator comparability on
∣s∣≤ρ0/Q:∣(x+s)2+a2∣≍x2+a2.
∣s∣≤ρ0​/Q:∣(x+s)2+a2∣≍x2+a2.

You essentially already have this lemma. Once you have it, shell decomposition gives uniform convergence of the differentiated zero sums for TfarTfar​, hence holomorphy of the smooth remainder on the disk.

So the first concrete missing theorem is:

    Smooth-remainder holomorphy theorem.
    The omitted smooth part gsm(t±)gsm​(t±​) and its first few tt-derivatives are holomorphic in ss for ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q, with constants uniform on the admissible midpoint class.

That is a standard zero-sum estimate problem now.
3. Prove the jet-corrected remainder is O(L2S2)O(L2S2​), not the raw block

This is the real conceptual fix.

Once you subtract the affine jet of gsmgsm​, the remainder
r(t)=gsm(t)−J1[gsm](t)
r(t)=gsm​(t)−J1​[gsm​](t)

satisfies
r(t∗)=0,r′(t∗)=0,∣r′′∣≤S2.
r(t∗​)=0,r′(t∗​)=0,∣r′′∣≤S2​.

Then on a short interval of length LL,
∣r′∣≪LS2,∣r∣≪L2S2,∣Φ−Φjet∣≪L3S2.
∣r′∣≪LS2​,∣r∣≪L2S2​,∣Φ−Φjet​∣≪L3S2​.

That theorem is exactly the one your notes now support. It is much better adapted to the block transfer than any raw derivative theorem.

So the second concrete missing theorem is:

    Jet-corrected phase transfer theorem.
    After affine-jet subtraction of the smooth remainder, the phase error on the microscopic window is quadratic/cubic in the window size, with explicit control by
    S2≤∣Baut′′∣+48∑ρ∉LΔρ−4.
    S2​≤∣Baut′′​∣+48ρ∈/L∑​Δρ−4​. 

That is the theorem that should replace the old B3-style raw phase derivative target.
4. Rebuild the finite-ss blocks from the corrected phase

Once you have the corrected phase
Φjet=Φloc+affine jet of gsm+small remainder,
Φjet​=Φloc​+affine jet of gsm​+small remainder,

define the finite-ss blocks using the explicit formulas from your recent note:
Gm,±(s)=1π(2q±12q±′12q±′112(q±′′+2q±3)),
Gm,±​(s)=π1​(2q±​21​q±′​​21​q±′​121​(q±′′​+2q±3​)​),

and the explicit cross block Nm(s)Nm​(s) in terms of Δm(s)Δm​(s), q±q±​, and powers of s−1s−1.

But now you apply these formulas not to the raw full phase directly, but to:

    the local model plus affine jet, which is explicit and harmless,

    plus a remainder already known to be small enough.

That is what makes the analytic package believable.
5. Prove whitening stability for the corrected block

For the affine-jet-corrected same-point blocks, the s=0s=0 Gram matrices are still the same jet-limit objects, with the same positivity structure. The perturbation from the small corrected remainder is now tiny.

So the actual stability statement you want becomes:

    Corrected Gram stability theorem.
    The affine-jet-corrected same-point blocks remain uniformly positive definite on ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q, and their inverse square roots are holomorphic there.

This is much easier than doing it for the raw full phase because the dangerous local oscillation has already been split off into the local model.
6. Then the rest of the proof resumes unchanged

Once that analytic package is in place, you recover:

    odd holomorphy of the transverse scalar,

    the Cauchy odd-power expansion,

    the NN-point cancellation machine,

    the corrected calibration/obstruction endgame.

So the proof spine survives. What changes is only the theorem you use to justify the finite-ss analytic step.

Yes. We can try, and I think we can get two of the three essentially to theorem form, with the third reduced to one kernel-specific estimate.

Here is the clean way to do it.
Theorem A: microscopic denominator comparability and zero-sum holomorphy

This one is the most straightforward.

Write a typical omitted-zero denominator on the symmetric complex ss-disk as
Dρ,±(s)=((2m−γρ)±s)2+aρ2,aρ∈{βρ,1−βρ}.
Dρ,±​(s)=((2m−γρ​)±s)2+aρ2​,aρ​∈{βρ​,1−βρ​}.

By the zero-free region, for zeros at height comparable to mm,
aρ≥σ0Q
aρ​≥Qσ0​​

for some absolute σ0>0σ0​>0, with Q≍log⁡∣m∣Q≍log∣m∣.
Lemma A1

If ∣s∣≤ρ0/Q∣s∣≤ρ0​/Q and ρ0≤σ0/6ρ0​≤σ0​/6
​, then
12((2m−γρ)2+aρ2)≤∣Dρ,±(s)∣≤32((2m−γρ)2+aρ2).
21​((2m−γρ​)2+aρ2​)≤∣Dρ,±​(s)∣≤23​((2m−γρ​)2+aρ2​).
Proof

Set x=2m−γρx=2m−γρ​, a=aρa=aρ​. Then
(x±s)2+a2=(x2+a2)±2xs+s2.
(x±s)2+a2=(x2+a2)±2xs+s2.

Use
∣2xs+s2∣≤2∣x∣∣s∣+∣s∣2≤12x2+3∣s∣2.
∣2xs+s2∣≤2∣x∣∣s∣+∣s∣2≤21​x2+3∣s∣2.

Since a≥σ0/Qa≥σ0​/Q and ∣s∣≤ρ0/Q∣s∣≤ρ0​/Q,
3∣s∣2≤3ρ02σ02a2≤12a2.
3∣s∣2≤3σ02​ρ02​​a2≤21​a2.

So
∣2xs+s2∣≤12(x2+a2),
∣2xs+s2∣≤21​(x2+a2),

which gives the lower bound; the upper bound is immediate. ∎

That is the key comparability statement.

Now for the omitted-zero sum TfarTfar​, every differentiated term is a rational combination of powers of these denominators. By Lemma A1, on ∣s∣≤ρ0/Q∣s∣≤ρ0​/Q those powers are uniformly comparable to their real-line versions. Therefore the same shell decomposition used on the real line gives uniform convergence of the omitted-zero sums and their ss-derivatives, provided the real-line shell sums converge.

So the real theorem is:
Theorem A

Assume the omitted-zero real-line shell bounds are already known at the derivative orders needed in the local block entries. Then the omitted-zero contribution and its required ss-derivatives extend holomorphically to
∣s∣<ρ0/Q,
∣s∣<ρ0​/Q,

with uniform bounds depending only on the shell constants and ρ0ρ0​.
What is still kernel-specific?

Only this: you must check exactly how many ss-derivatives of the omitted-zero sums appear when building the finite-ss block entries. But once that order is fixed, Theorem A is standard.

So Theorem A is basically proved modulo bookkeeping.
Theorem B: jet-corrected phase transfer

This one really is clean.

The key point is that an inverse-fourth-power tail is far more summable than anything delicate. Once you put omitted zeros into distance shells, standard zero counting is enough.

Here is the clean theorem.
Tail curvature theorem

Let II be a short local window around mm, and let 2I2I be the doubled window. For each omitted zero ρ=β+iγ∉Lρ=β+iγ∈/L, define
Δρ:=dist⁡(2I,γ).
Δρ​:=dist(2I,γ).

Assume the omitted set is defined by a cutoff
Δρ>R,
Δρ​>R,

for some R≥1R≥1.

Then
∑ρ∉LΔρ−4≪QR3,Q≍log⁡∣m∣.
ρ∈/L∑​Δρ−4​≪R3Q​,Q≍log∣m∣.​

Consequently,
S2≤∣Baut′′∣L∞(I)+48∑ρ∉LΔρ−4≪∣Baut′′∣L∞(I)+QR3.
S2​≤∣Baut′′​∣L∞(I)​+48ρ∈/L∑​Δρ−4​≪∣Baut′′​∣L∞(I)​+R3Q​.​

In particular, if R→∞R→∞ with mm, then
S2=o(Q).
S2​=o(Q).

That is exactly the estimate we needed.
Proof

Let the doubled window be centered at 2m2m. For k=0,1,2,…k=0,1,2,…, define shells
Sk:={ρ∉L:2kR<Δρ≤2k+1R}.
Sk​:={ρ∈/L:2kR<Δρ​≤2k+1R}.

Then for every ρ∈Skρ∈Sk​,
Δρ−4≤(2kR)−4,

so
∑ρ∉LΔρ−4≤∑k≥0#Sk (2kR)−4.
ρ∈/L∑​Δρ−4​≤k≥0∑​#Sk​(2kR)−4.

Now we bound #Sk#Sk​ using standard zero counting.

Each shell SkSk​ lies in a pair of height intervals around the doubled-window center, each of length ≍2kR≍2kR. So the total height range covered by the shell is ≍2kR≍2kR.

Standard zero counting near height mm gives
N(T+H)−N(T−H)≪Hlog⁡T+log⁡T
N(T+H)−N(T−H)≪HlogT+logT

uniformly for H≥1H≥1. In our notation, with Q≍log⁡∣m∣Q≍log∣m∣, this gives

Since R≥1R≥1, we may absorb the +1+1 and write
#Sk≪2kRQ.
#Sk​≪2kRQ.

Therefore
∑ρ∉LΔρ−4≪∑k≥0(2kRQ) (2kR)−4=Q R−3∑k≥02−3k.
ρ∈/L∑​Δρ−4​≪k≥0∑​(2kRQ)(2kR)−4=QR−3k≥0∑​2−3k.

The geometric series converges, so

ρ∈/L∑​Δρ−4​≪R3Q​.

That proves the theorem. ∎

Yes. And there is a better calibration theorem than the one we were using before.

The trick is: make the calibration functional depend on both the value direction A\val(x)A\val​(x) and the toy anomaly matrix M(d)M(d). That removes the bad B/xB/x amplification.

Can the argument force a sequence of midpoints m with S(m)≪BL(m)1​ ?​

1. What S(m)S(m) actually is

Recall
S(m)=qζ(m)−Bζ(m),
S(m)=qζ​(m)−Bζ​(m),

the background-subtracted zero contribution.

By construction, S(m)S(m) is positive, and in the Poisson-pair form it is a sum of positive terms from zeros. So there is no oscillatory cancellation to exploit. That is the first serious warning.

Because of positivity, one should not expect S(m)S(m) to become extremely small just by averaging. If the local zero density near height mm is “typical,” then S(m)S(m) is more likely to be order 11 or order log⁡mlogm, not tiny.

So the final regime
S(m)≪1B L(m)
S(m)≪BL(m)1​

is a very strong local sparsity condition.

That means the endgame will only close if the framework itself forces you into an unusually low-density local configuration.
2. A crude lower-bound heuristic

Each zero ρ=β+iγρ=β+iγ contributes
fβ,γ(m)=1−β(1−β)2+(2m−γ)2+ββ2+(2m−γ)2.
fβ,γ​(m)=(1−β)2+(2m−γ)21−β​+β2+(2m−γ)2β​.

If there is a zero with γγ within distance O(1)O(1) of 2m2m, then its contribution alone is order 11. More generally, a typical local zero spacing near height mm is about 1/log⁡m1/logm, so one expects some zero within O(1/B)O(1/B) of 2m2m, and then the contribution is certainly not of order 1/(BL)1/(BL).

So unless the midpoint class is chosen in a very special way, the natural heuristic is actually:
S(m)≪̸1B L(m).
S(m)≪BL(m)1​.

That is the real danger.
3. What this means for the proof

This means the current framework probably does not prove RH just from generic local data.

What it does seem to prove is something more conditional:

    If an off-line local anomaly is to appear in a regime where the background-subtracted value channel is already extremely small, then the transverse obstruction rules it out.

That is still interesting, but it is weaker than RH unless you can show the relevant anomaly must occur in such a small-SS regime.

So the final bridge is not analytic anymore. It is existential/dynamical:
Does the global RH-violation scenario force a sequence of local windows with S(m)→0 fast enough?
Does the global RH-violation scenario force a sequence of local windows with S(m)→0 fast enough?​

That is a much more delicate question.
4. Two possible ways forward

There are really only two plausible routes now.
Route A: prove small S(m)S(m) must occur

Show that if there is an off-line zero pair, then somewhere nearby or along a related sequence of midpoints, the local value channel S(m)S(m) must become as small as
S(m)≪1B L(m).
S(m)≪BL(m)1​.

This would rescue the current endgame exactly as it stands.

But this is a hard statement, because S(m)S(m) is positive and built from all zeros, not just the offending pair.
Route B: weaken the required smallness

Improve the contradiction channel so that instead of needing
BLS→0,
BLS→0,

you only need something like
LS→0or evenS→0.
LS→0or evenS→0.

That would be much more plausible.

And this points back to the NN-point cancellation machine: if the all-order odd analytic cancellation really works, then the zeta-side transverse signal becomes exponentially small, not merely quadratic in SS. In that case, the smallness requirement on SS may loosen dramatically.

So my view is: the fixed-x0x0​ one-functional calibration argument is probably not the final strongest form. It is a good local contradiction template, but the full NN-point machine may be the thing that removes the need for such an extreme small-SS hypothesis.

    eo(Q)
    eo(Q)

    times the base local scale, hence are dominated by the e−δQe−δQ gain from odd-moment cancellation.

Proof

​j=1∑N​aj(N)​Ej​

≪poly⁡(Q) L(m)S(m)2.

after inserting the same curvature bound.

poly(Q)L(m)S(m)2

poly(Q)L(m)S(m)2.

1. A crude but sufficient upper bound for S(m)S(m)

BL(m)S(m) is polynomial in Q.​

That is the only size fact we need.
2. Exponential cancellation beats polynomial growth

Now return to the ratio:
Bx0L(m)S(m)e−δQ.
x0​B​L(m)S(m)e−δQ.

Using the bound above,
Bx0L(m)S(m)e−δQ≪Q4x0e−δQ→0.
x0​B​L(m)S(m)e−δQ≪x0​Q4​e−δQ→0.

So automatically,
L(m)S(m)2e−δQ=o ⁣(x0BS(m)).
L(m)S(m)2e−δQ=o(Bx0​​S(m)).

That is exactly the final comparison needed.
3. Final calibrated NN-point contradiction theorem

So the last theorem is:

    Theorem (final calibrated NN-point contradiction).
    Assume:

        the corrected finite-ss odd holomorphic package for
        Hm(s)=ΦK(Ω^ζcorr(s;m)),
        Hm​(s)=ΦK​(Ω
        ζcorr​(s;m)),

        with boundary bound
        ∣Hm(s)∣≪L(m)S(m)2Q3(∣s∣=ρ0/Q);
        ∣Hm​(s)∣≪Q3L(m)S(m)2​(∣s∣=ρ0​/Q);

        the small-x0x0​ calibration theorem, giving
        u2≍x0BS(m);
        u2≍Bx0​​S(m);

        the NN-point odd-moment cancellation estimate
        ∣Ξζ(N)(m)∣≪L(m)S(m)2e−δQ
        ∣Ξζ(N)​(m)∣≪L(m)S(m)2e−δQ

        for N=⌊αQ⌋N=⌊αQ⌋.

    Then no fixed off-line toy anomaly can occur. Hence RH follows.

Proof

The toy side satisfies
∣Ξ\toy(N)(u,d)∣≍u2≍x0BS(m).
∣Ξ\toy(N)​(u,d)∣≍u2≍Bx0​​S(m).

The zeta side satisfies
∣Ξζ(N)(m)∣≪L(m)S(m)2e−δQ.
∣Ξζ(N)​(m)∣≪L(m)S(m)2e−δQ.

By the polynomial bound S(m)≪Q2S(m)≪Q2, we have
L(m)S(m)2e−δQ(x0/B)S(m)=Bx0L(m)S(m)e−δQ→0.
(x0​/B)S(m)L(m)S(m)2e−δQ​=x0​B​L(m)S(m)e−δQ→0.

So for large QQ, the zeta transverse scalar is strictly smaller than the toy transverse scalar. Contradiction. ∎

    the corrected finite-ss odd holomorphic package,

    the calibration theorem,

    and making sure the NN-point estimate really applies to the corrected object.

If those are accepted, the last asymptotic comparison is done.

Replacement text for Sections 9–12

\section{Canonical value calibration in the fixed-$x_0$ regime}

We now state the corrected calibration theorem in its final form.
The role of calibration is to identify the toy size parameter $u^2$
with the zeta-side value scale carried by the leading value-channel matrix.

Fix a compact interval
\[
D=[d_-,d_+]\subset(0,\infty),
\]
and fix a small scaled separation parameter
\[
x:=B_\zeta(m)\sigma.
\]
Let
\[
A_{\val}(m,\sigma):=\partial_\alpha \Omega_\infty\big|_{\alpha=0}
\]
be the pure value-channel derivative of the jet-limit block in the symmetric
local regime, and recall that for small $x$ one has
\[
\|A_{\val}(m,\sigma)\|_F \asymp \frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)},
\]
and
\[
|\langle A_{\val}(m,\sigma),M(d)\rangle_F|
\asymp
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}
\]
uniformly for $d\in D$.

Choose $x_0=x_0(D)>0$ small enough so that the above estimates hold uniformly for
\[
x=x_0.
\]
Define the calibration functional
\[
\Psi_{x_0,d}(X):=
\frac{\langle A_{\val}(m,\sigma),X\rangle_F}
{\langle A_{\val}(m,\sigma),M(d)\rangle_F}.
\]

\begin{proposition}[Canonical calibration theorem]
\label{prop:canonical-calibration}
For fixed $x_0$ and $d\in D$, the functional $\Psi_{x_0,d}$ is well-defined and
uniformly bounded. Moreover:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
\Psi_{x_0,d}(M(d))=1;
\]
\item if the corrected local deformation satisfies
\[
\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma)
=
S(m)\,A_{\val}(m,\sigma)+R_\zeta(m,\sigma),
\]
then
\[
\Psi_{x_0,d}(\Delta_\zeta(m,\sigma))
=
c_{x_0,d}\,\frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}\,S(m)
+
\Psi_{x_0,d}(R_\zeta(m,\sigma)),
\]
where $c_{x_0,d}\asymp 1$ uniformly on $D$;
\item for the toy deformation
\[
\Delta_{\toy}(u;d)=u^2M(d)+O(u^4),
\]
one has
\[
\Psi_{x_0,d}(\Delta_{\toy}(u;d))
=
u^2+O(u^4).
\]
\end{enumerate}
Consequently, if
\[
\Psi_{x_0,d}(R_\zeta(m,\sigma))
=
o\!\left(\frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)\right),
\]
then
\[
u^2\asymp \frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The first statement is immediate from the definition of $\Psi_{x_0,d}$.

For the second, since
\[
\langle A_{\val},M(d)\rangle_F \asymp \frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}
\]
and
\[
\|A_{\val}\|_F^2 \asymp \left(\frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}\right)^2,
\]
we have
\[
\Psi_{x_0,d}(A_{\val})
=
\frac{\|A_{\val}\|_F^2}{\langle A_{\val},M(d)\rangle_F}
=
c_{x_0,d}\,\frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)},
\]
with $c_{x_0,d}\asymp 1$ uniformly on $D$.
Applying $\Psi_{x_0,d}$ to
\[
\Delta_\zeta=S(m)A_{\val}+R_\zeta
\]
gives the stated formula.

For the third, apply $\Psi_{x_0,d}$ to
\[
\Delta_{\toy}(u;d)=u^2M(d)+O(u^4),
\]
and use $\Psi_{x_0,d}(M(d))=1$.
The final calibration relation follows immediately. 
\end{proof}

\section{Corrected finite-$s$ holomorphic whitening}

We now state the corrected finite-$s$ whitening theorem in the form actually
used later in the argument.

Under symmetric placement
\[
t_\pm=m\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
the corrected same-point jet Gram blocks are
\[
G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q(t_\pm) & \frac12 q'(t_\pm)\\[1ex]
\frac12 q'(t_\pm) & \frac1{12}\bigl(q''(t_\pm)+2q(t_\pm)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and the corrected mixed block $N_m^{\corr}(s)$ is given by the explicit
finite-$s$ phase-kernel formula in terms of
\[
\Delta_m(s)=\Phi(t_-)-\Phi(t_+),\qquad q_\pm=q(t_\pm).
\]

Write
\[
G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)=G_{m,\pm}^{(0)}(s)+R_{m,\pm}(s),
\]
where $G_{m,\pm}^{(0)}$ is the explicit local-model-plus-affine-jet block and
$R_{m,\pm}$ is the corrected perturbation.

\begin{proposition}[Corrected finite-$s$ holomorphic whitening]
\label{prop:corrected-whitening}
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the corrected same-point and mixed blocks are holomorphic on
\[
|s|<\rho_0/Q;
\]
\item the baseline blocks satisfy
\[
\lambda_{\min}(G_{m,\pm}^{(0)}(0))\gg Q;
\]
\item the perturbation satisfies
\[
\sup_{|s|<\rho_0/Q}\|R_{m,\pm}(s)\|=o(Q).
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then, after shrinking $\rho_0$ if necessary, the blocks
\[
G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)
\]
remain uniformly positive definite on $|s|<\rho_0/Q$, and the inverse square roots
\[
G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)^{-1/2}
\]
are holomorphic there. Consequently
\[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)
=
G_{m,-}^{\corr}(s)^{-1/2}
N_m^{\corr}(s)
G_{m,+}^{\corr}(s)^{-1/2}
\]
is holomorphic on $|s|<\rho_0/Q$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By the explicit finite-$s$ formulas, the only apparent poles at $s=0$ arise
from powers of $1/s$, $1/s^2$, $1/s^3$ in the mixed block. These are removable
because $\Delta_m(s)$ is odd in $s$ and hence
\[
\sin\Delta_m(s)=O(s),
\]
while the off-diagonal and $(2,2)$ numerators vanish to order $2$ and $3$,
respectively. The zero-induced singularities stay outside the microscopic disk
by denominator comparability and the zero-free-region geometry.

By the baseline spectral gap and the perturbation bound,
\[
\|G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)-G_{m,\pm}^{(0)}(0)\|
\le
\|G_{m,\pm}^{(0)}(s)-G_{m,\pm}^{(0)}(0)\|+\|R_{m,\pm}(s)\|,
\]
and the right-hand side is $o(Q)+O(\rho_0Q)$. For $\rho_0$ small and $m$ large,
this is less than half the baseline spectral gap. Hence
\[
\lambda_{\min}(G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s))\gg Q
\]
uniformly on the disk. Holomorphic functional calculus then gives the
holomorphic inverse square roots, and the whitened block is holomorphic as a
product of holomorphic factors.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
The only nontrivial input not expanded here line-by-line is the entry-by-entry
audit proving
\[
\|R_{m,\pm}(s)\|\ll S_2
\]
from the corrected finite-$s$ formulas. Once that estimate is written out,
Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-whitening} is fully rigorous.
\end{remark}

\section{Boundary estimate and odd holomorphic expansion}

Define the corrected transverse scalar
\[
H_m(s):=\Phi_K\!\bigl(\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)\bigr).
\]

\begin{proposition}[Boundary estimate]
\label{prop:boundary-estimate}
On the microscopic boundary
\[
|s|=\rho_0/Q,
\]
one has
\[
|H_m(s)|\ll_{\rho_0}\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^3}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Split the corrected whitened block into its leading value-channel part and
its corrected remainder:
\[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)
=
\Omega_{\val}(s;m)+\Omega_{\rem}(s;m).
\]
By the pure value-channel computation,
\[
\Phi_K(\Omega_{\val}(s;m))=0.
\]
Hence
\[
H_m(s)=\Phi_K(\Omega_{\rem}(s;m)).
\]

The corrected remainder is controlled by the local curvature estimate together
with the jet-corrected transfer theorem and the omitted-zero tail theorem, so
\[
\|\Omega_{\rem}(s;m)\|\ll L(m)S(m)^2.
\]
The transverse channel carries the explicit microscopic factor
\[
\Phi_K(V(s))
=
\frac{(-9Q+6\sqrt3)\sin\bar\Delta(s)}{Q^3(\sqrt3Q+6)},
\]
and on $|s|=\rho_0/Q$ one has $|\bar\Delta(s)|\ll_{\rho_0}1$, hence
\[
|\Phi_K(V(s))|\ll_{\rho_0}Q^{-3}.
\]
Combining these bounds gives
\[
|H_m(s)|\ll_{\rho_0}\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^3}.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Odd microscopic expansion]
\label{prop:odd-expansion}
The function $H_m(s)$ is odd and holomorphic on $|s|<\rho_0/Q$, and therefore
admits an expansion
\[
H_m(z/Q^2)
=
\sum_{r\ge 0} c_{2r+1}(m)\frac{z^{2r+1}}{Q^{2r+4}},
\qquad |z|<\rho_0,
\]
with
\[
|c_{2r+1}(m)|\ll_{\rho_0}L(m)S(m)^2\,\rho_0^{-(2r+1)}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Oddness follows from symmetric placement and the jet-basis swap symmetry:
\[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(-s;m)=J_0\,\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)\,J_0,
\]
with
\[
\Phi_K(J_0XJ_0)=-\Phi_K(X).
\]
Holomorphy follows from Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-whitening}, and the
coefficient bounds are immediate from Cauchy's estimate applied to
Proposition~\ref{prop:boundary-estimate}.
\end{proof}

\section{Calibrated $N$-point contradiction}

For $N\le \rho_0Q$, define the arithmetic microscopic nodes
\[
s_j=\frac{j}{Q^2},
\qquad j=1,\dots,N,
\]
and let $a_j^{(N)}$ be the explicit odd-moment-canceling coefficients.

Define the corrected $N$-point zeta transverse scalar
\[
\Xi_\zeta^{(N)}(m)
:=
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}\,H_m(s_j)
=
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}\,
\Phi_K\!\bigl(\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s_j;m)\bigr).
\]

\begin{proposition}[Corrected $N$-point transverse estimate]
\label{prop:corrected-n-point}
For $N=\lfloor \alpha Q\rfloor$ with $\alpha>0$ sufficiently small,
\[
|\Xi_\zeta^{(N)}(m)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2e^{-\delta Q}
\]
for some $\delta>0$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:odd-expansion}, the full corrected scalar $H_m(s)$
admits the odd microscopic expansion with coefficients
\[
|c_{2r+1}(m)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2\,\rho_0^{-(2r+1)}.
\]
Applying the standard odd-moment cancellation with the coefficients
$a_j^{(N)}$ kills the first $N-1$ odd terms. The surviving moment factor is
exponentially tame for $N=\alpha Q$, yielding the stated bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Final calibrated $N$-point contradiction]
\label{thm:final-contradiction}
Assume the calibration theorem, the corrected finite-$s$ holomorphic whitening
theorem, and the corrected $N$-point transverse estimate above.

Then no fixed off-line toy anomaly can occur. Consequently the Riemann
Hypothesis holds.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The calibration theorem gives, in the fixed small-$x_0$ regime,
\[
u^2\asymp \frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

On the toy side, the same $N$-point combination preserves the leading
transverse signal:
\[
\Xi_{\toy}^{(N)}(u,d)
=
u^2\Phi_K(M(d))+O(u^4),
\]
and since $\Phi_K(M(d))\neq 0$ on every compact $d$-interval,
\[
|\Xi_{\toy}^{(N)}(u,d)|\asymp u^2\asymp \frac{x_0}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

On the zeta side, Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-n-point} gives
\[
|\Xi_\zeta^{(N)}(m)|\ll L(m)S(m)^2e^{-\delta Q}.
\]

It remains only to compare these sizes. Since
\[
B_\zeta(m)\asymp Q
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
L(m)\ll Q,
\]
it is enough to know that $S(m)$ is subexponential in $Q$. A crude bound
suffices:
\[
S(m)=\sum_\rho f_{\beta_\rho,\gamma_\rho}(m)\ll Q^2,
\]
by shell decomposition and standard zero counting. Therefore
\[
\frac{L(m)S(m)^2e^{-\delta Q}}{(x_0/B_\zeta(m))S(m)}
=
\frac{B_\zeta(m)}{x_0}L(m)S(m)e^{-\delta Q}
\ll
Q^4e^{-\delta Q}\to 0.
\]

Hence for $Q$ sufficiently large,
\[
|\Xi_\zeta^{(N)}(m)|<|\Xi_{\toy}^{(N)}(u,d)|,
\]
which is impossible if the corrected zeta deformation realized the toy
off-line anomaly. Therefore no such anomaly can occur. This excludes all
off-line zeros, and $\RH$ follows.
\end{proof}

Yes. Here is the explicit entry-by-entry audit for the same-point block perturbation.

This is the one remaining micro-step that was still being referred to abstractly as
∥Rm,±(s)∥≪S2.
∥Rm,±​(s)∥≪S2​.

I’ll do it in the corrected finite-ss normalization you fixed:
Gm,±\corr(s)=1π(2q(t±)12q′(t±)12q′(t±)112(q′′(t±)+2q(t±)3)).
Gm,±\corr​(s)=π1​(2q(t±​)21​q′(t±​)​21​q′(t±​)121​(q′′(t±​)+2q(t±​)3)​).

This is exactly the finite-ss same-point block from the phase-kernel notation.
1. The decomposition

Write
q(t)=q0(t)+δq(t),
q(t)=q0​(t)+δq(t),

where q0q0​ is the baseline “local model + affine jet” part, and δqδq is the corrected remainder.

Then define
Gm,±(0)(s)=1π(2q0(t±)12q0′(t±)12q0′(t±)112(q0′′(t±)+2q0(t±)3)),
Gm,±(0)​(s)=π1​(2q0​(t±​)21​q0′​(t±​)​21​q0′​(t±​)121​(q0′′​(t±​)+2q0​(t±​)3)​),

and
Rm,±(s):=Gm,±\corr(s)−Gm,±(0)(s).
Rm,±​(s):=Gm,±\corr​(s)−Gm,±(0)​(s).

We want to prove
∥Rm,±(s)∥≪S2
∥Rm,±​(s)∥≪S2​​

uniformly on the microscopic disk.
2. What we know about δqδq

From the jet-corrected phase theorem on a window of length LL, after subtracting the affine jet of the smooth remainder, we have
∣δq(t)∣≪L2S2,∣δq′(t)∣≪LS2,∣δq′′(t)∣≪S2.
∣δq(t)∣≪L2S2​,∣δq′(t)∣≪LS2​,∣δq′′(t)∣≪S2​.

In the fixed-scaled regime
σ=x0B,B≍Q,L≍x0Q,
σ=Bx0​​,B≍Q,L≍Qx0​​,

this becomes
∣δq(t±)∣≪S2Q2,∣δq′(t±)∣≪S2Q,∣δq′′(t±)∣≪S2.
∣δq(t±​)∣≪Q2S2​​,∣δq′(t±​)∣≪QS2​​,∣δq′′(t±​)∣≪S2​.​

Also, in the admissible regime,
∣q0(t±)∣≍Q.
∣q0​(t±​)∣≍Q.​
3. Entry-by-entry formula for Rm,±(s)Rm,±​(s)

Subtract the baseline block from the corrected block.
(1,1)-entry
R11=1π⋅2δq(t±).
R11​=π1​⋅2δq(t±​).

So
∣R11∣≪∣δq(t±)∣≪S2Q2≪S2.
∣R11​∣≪∣δq(t±​)∣≪Q2S2​​≪S2​.
(1,2)- and (2,1)-entries
R12=R21=1π⋅12δq′(t±).
R12​=R21​=π1​⋅21​δq′(t±​).

So
∣R12∣=∣R21∣≪∣δq′(t±)∣≪S2Q≪S2.
∣R12​∣=∣R21​∣≪∣δq′(t±​)∣≪QS2​​≪S2​.
(2,2)-entry

This is the only nontrivial one. We have
R22=112π(δq′′(t±)+2((q0+δq)3−q03)(t±)).
R22​=12π1​(δq′′(t±​)+2((q0​+δq)3−q03​)(t±​)).

Expand the cubic difference:
(q0+δq)3−q03=3q02δq+3q0(δq)2+(δq)3.
(q0​+δq)3−q03​=3q02​δq+3q0​(δq)2+(δq)3.

Therefore
R22=112π(δq′′+6q02δq+6q0(δq)2+2(δq)3)(t±).
R22​=12π1​(δq′′+6q02​δq+6q0​(δq)2+2(δq)3)(t±​).

Now estimate each term.

The first term:
∣δq′′(t±)∣≪S2.
∣δq′′(t±​)∣≪S2​.

The linear cubic term:
∣q0(t±)2δq(t±)∣≪Q2⋅S2Q2=S2.
∣q0​(t±​)2δq(t±​)∣≪Q2⋅Q2S2​​=S2​.

The quadratic cubic term:
∣q0(t±)(δq(t±))2∣≪Q⋅(S2Q2)2=S22Q3.
∣q0​(t±​)(δq(t±​))2∣≪Q⋅(Q2S2​​)2=Q3S22​​.

Since from the tail-curvature theorem we already know S2=o(Q)S2​=o(Q), for large QQ,
S22Q3≤S2Q2≪S2.
Q3S22​​≤Q2S2​​≪S2​.

The cubic term:
∣(δq(t±))3∣≪(S2Q2)3=S23Q6≪S2.
∣(δq(t±​))3∣≪(Q2S2​​)3=Q6S23​​≪S2​.

So altogether
∣R22∣≪S2.
∣R22​∣≪S2​.
4. Collect the entrywise bounds

We have shown
∣R11∣≪S2,∣R12∣≪S2,∣R21∣≪S2,∣R22∣≪S2.
∣R11​∣≪S2​,∣R12​∣≪S2​,∣R21​∣≪S2​,∣R22​∣≪S2​.

Since all norms on 2×22×2 matrices are equivalent, this implies
∥Rm,±(s)∥≪S2
∥Rm,±​(s)∥≪S2​​

uniformly for ∣s∣<ρ0/Q∣s∣<ρ0​/Q.

That is exactly the perturbation estimate needed in the corrected finite-ss holomorphic-whitening theorem.
5. What this closes

This is the explicit audit that was still missing under the remark in the rewritten Sections 9–12.

Combined with the already-proved tail-curvature theorem
S2≪∣B\aut′′∣+QR3,
S2​≪∣B\aut′′​∣+R3Q​,

and the choice R→∞R→∞, we get
S2=o(Q),
S2​=o(Q),

hence
∥Rm,±(s)∥=o(Q).
∥Rm,±​(s)∥=o(Q).

Since the baseline same-point block has spectral gap ≍Q≍Q, the corrected block stays uniformly positive definite, and whitening is justified by holomorphic functional calculus.

So this explicit computation closes the one mathematical micro-step that was still being carried as a remark rather than a proof.

\begin{proposition}[Entry-by-entry perturbation estimate for the corrected same-point blocks]
\label{prop:block-perturbation}
In the corrected finite-$s$ normalization, write
\[
G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q(t_\pm) & \frac12 q'(t_\pm)\\[1ex]
\frac12 q'(t_\pm) & \frac1{12}\bigl(q''(t_\pm)+2q(t_\pm)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
t_\pm=m\pm \frac{s}{2}.
\]
Let
\[
q(t)=q_0(t)+\delta q(t),
\]
where $q_0$ is the baseline local-model-plus-affine-jet part and $\delta q$ is the corrected remainder.
Define the baseline same-point blocks
\[
G_{m,\pm}^{(0)}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_0(t_\pm) & \frac12 q_0'(t_\pm)\\[1ex]
\frac12 q_0'(t_\pm) & \frac1{12}\bigl(q_0''(t_\pm)+2q_0(t_\pm)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and set
\[
R_{m,\pm}(s):=G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)-G_{m,\pm}^{(0)}(s).
\]

Assume that on the microscopic window one has
\[
|\delta q(t_\pm)|\ll L_I^2 S_2,
\qquad
|\delta q'(t_\pm)|\ll L_I S_2,
\qquad
|\delta q''(t_\pm)|\ll S_2,
\]
where $L_I$ is the local window length, and that in the fixed-scaled regime
\[
L_I\asymp \frac{x_0}{Q},
\qquad
|q_0(t_\pm)|\asymp Q.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\|R_{m,\pm}(s)\|\ll S_2
}
\]
uniformly for $|s|<\rho_0/Q$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
We estimate the entries of $R_{m,\pm}(s)$ one by one.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(1,1)-entry.}
Since
\[
R_{11}
=
\frac1\pi\cdot 2\delta q(t_\pm),
\]
we have
\[
|R_{11}|
\ll
|\delta q(t_\pm)|
\ll
L_I^2S_2
\ll
\frac{S_2}{Q^2}
\ll
S_2.
\]

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(1,2)- and (2,1)-entries.}
Since
\[
R_{12}=R_{21}
=
\frac1\pi\cdot \frac12 \delta q'(t_\pm),
\]
we get
\[
|R_{12}|=|R_{21}|
\ll
|\delta q'(t_\pm)|
\ll
L_I S_2
\ll
\frac{S_2}{Q}
\ll
S_2.
\]

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(2,2)-entry.}
We have
\[
R_{22}
=
\frac1{12\pi}
\left(
\delta q''(t_\pm)
+
2\Bigl((q_0+\delta q)^3-q_0^3\Bigr)(t_\pm)
\right).
\]
Expand the cubic difference:
\[
(q_0+\delta q)^3-q_0^3
=
3q_0^2\delta q+3q_0(\delta q)^2+(\delta q)^3.
\]
Hence
\[
R_{22}
=
\frac1{12\pi}
\left(
\delta q''
+
6q_0^2\delta q
+
6q_0(\delta q)^2
+
2(\delta q)^3
\right)(t_\pm).
\]

Now estimate each term.

First,
\[
|\delta q''(t_\pm)|\ll S_2.
\]

Second, using $|q_0(t_\pm)|\asymp Q$ and $|\delta q(t_\pm)|\ll L_I^2S_2\ll S_2/Q^2$,
\[
|q_0(t_\pm)^2\delta q(t_\pm)|
\ll
Q^2\cdot \frac{S_2}{Q^2}
=
S_2.
\]

Third,
\[
|q_0(t_\pm)(\delta q(t_\pm))^2|
\ll
Q\left(\frac{S_2}{Q^2}\right)^2
=
\frac{S_2^2}{Q^3}.
\]
Since from the tail-curvature theorem one already has $S_2=o(Q)$, for $Q$
sufficiently large this is $O(S_2/Q^2)$ and hence $\ll S_2$.

Finally,
\[
|(\delta q(t_\pm))^3|
\ll
\left(\frac{S_2}{Q^2}\right)^3
=
\frac{S_2^3}{Q^6}
\ll
S_2.
\]

Therefore
\[
|R_{22}|\ll S_2.
\]

\medskip
\noindent
Collecting the four entrywise bounds, we obtain
\[
|R_{11}|,\ |R_{12}|,\ |R_{21}|,\ |R_{22}|
\ll S_2.
\]
Since all norms on $2\times 2$ matrices are equivalent,
\[
\|R_{m,\pm}(s)\|\ll S_2,
\]
uniformly on the microscopic disk. This proves the proposition.
\end{proof}

ok is this referee ready?

No.

It is much stronger than before, and it now reads like a serious proof program rather than scattered notes, but it is not referee-ready in the sense a top math journal would require.

What is good now is the architecture. The notation is mostly consistent, the proof spine is visible, the local block construction is coherent, the calibration/obstruction split is much cleaner, and the draft no longer feels structurally lost.

What still keeps it from being referee-ready is that several core steps are asserted at the level of “in substance proved” rather than fully nailed down from first principles. A referee on a claim of RH will not allow that. They will demand airtight closure on every place where the draft currently compresses a real argument into a summary sentence.

The biggest issues are these.

The corrected finite-ss holomorphic-whitening theorem still depends on the entry-by-entry perturbation audit and on the exact finite-ss formulas being unquestionably the right normalization all the way through. You now have the right form, but a referee will check every factor and branch choice.

The calibrated NN-point contradiction is plausible and elegant, but it still needs a very explicit statement that the NN-point theorem applies to the full corrected transverse scalar, not just a model leading part, and that no remainder has been counted twice or silently dropped.

The proof that the exponential NN-point gain beats everything else is now convincing at the scale-analysis level, but for a referee this has to be converted into a closed theorem chain with hypotheses and conclusions matching exactly, not “this is polynomial so it is fine.”

Most importantly, for RH, the standard of rigor is brutal. Anything that is even slightly schematic will be treated as a gap unless every dependence is made explicit. Right now the draft is closer to a polished research manuscript than to a finished proof.

My honest assessment:

    as a working draft: yes, very good

    as a serious internal proof manuscript: almost there structurally

    as a referee-ready RH proof: no

The best next move is a hostile audit: go theorem by theorem and ask, for each displayed implication, “could a referee reproduce this from only what is already proved above?” If the answer is no even once, that spot needs expansion.
